**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `14:24:36` **jimcollinson** said:

It's full e2e, and data stored is quantum secure thanks to the self-encryption algo. 

SNT isn't a privacy coin, and shouldn't be thought of as such — it runs the market for trading spare resources and storage and is super efficient for that, (and can also be used as a highly parallelisable payment network) but the key is that there is no tie between the tokens you spend, and the data your store using them… air-gapping the data on the network.

Yeah, there are for sure some privacy enhancements—say for those squeamish about putting their whole financial history out there on a blockchain—but its not a zCash/Monero alternative. There is still a graph there, and the DLT.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1212419879685328906)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `15:27:40` **jimcollinson** said:

When you are using a client to read or upload data to the network, no, you don't need to use Tor to enhance your privacy. That's because all data is chunked and encrypted with the hash of itself, and it's always in this state before it leaves your machine an hits the network. No passwords or keys leave the machine either. And all data i flight is encrypted, and looks is just like all other encrypted data. The bonus there is that the Network get net neutrality thrown in for free!

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1212420866646868020)

We are going to have one coupling in the external markets between EUR (and other currencies) and SNT, internally (unlike other crypto coins) we are going to have a coupling between SNT and many more services. 3. On (internet connected) local devices there are the usual threats you should be aware of
4. Secure local enclaves FTW, but beyond the needs of most people

## Friday, 2024-03-01

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `11:08:59` **jimcollinson** said:

There is. You see nodes hold a randomly assigned store of chunks. These chunks get moved and shuffled across the network to and from groups of nodes as the Network grows and as other nodes come and go. So nodes are rewarded over time even when they are full… it's not a case of: fill up, get paid, and then that's it. Nodes are rewarded for supplying the network over time. 

So if you are in and supplying, you can earn, stop, and you don't.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1213080543869018142)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `11:12:43` **jimcollinson** said:

There are a number of economic mechanisms at play to support the perpetual data proposition (probs better laid out in a longer form post) but in brief it's a combo of:

- Kryder's Law (and Moore's law)
- Data Compression
- Growth of Consumer Devices and Internet Connectivity
- De-duplication
- Emissions curve
- A few other bits

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1213081483997093908)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `11:14:32` **jimcollinson** said:

But I think it's worth also pondering the reason _why_ we have perpetual data… why the network (and all of us) should care and work together to provide it. Why is it a human need?

Because you don't have true autonomy over your digital life if you have to keep on paying the bills.

This is true even of many "decentralised" services! You are beholden to ongoing contract renegotiations and uptime of individual operators. This should be taken care of—autonomously—by the Network.

This is why we can provide true digital sovereignty.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1213081940257669204)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `19:22:38` **jimcollinson** said:

For nodes (which can just be standard consumer devices BTW not the enterprise data centre behemoths required by many decentralised networks) it really just means storage space, plus a little RAM, and bandwidth serve the data when required.

But there is another, less discussed aspect, which is the Network rewarding _creative_ resource. That's apps and code that operate on the Network, any ultimately _any_ data on it too.

While this won't be early days, there have long been plans and designs (on top of payments via token commerce user-to-user, direct to artist/dev style) for the Network itself to distribute these rewards autonomously. Pretty cool.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1213204776586706994)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `19:30:15` **jimcollinson** said:

And then there are other (seemingly minor features) that could add up to quite a big deal, that I get excited about quite a lot.

Like the ability to send payment and messages to _any data_ on the network. So think of that like a way to send a _superchat_ to any bit of data on the internet. 

Like a meme, but don't know who made it originally, and wanna say thanks? Send a tip and a message to the owner _via_ the data address.

Could be for anything. a bit of code you found useful, a song, a comment… Network wide! Or scoop up a whole site and pay to all nested contributors all in one go!

Could be the basis of some _REALLY_ interesting tokenomics meets socials. No reason it couldn't end up 'cross chain' either.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1213206689960955944)

## Saturday, 2024-03-02

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `15:56:17` **jimcollinson** said:

There are many, many verticals that the Network can serve. Many of them consumer-facing, but many won't need to pass the "supermarket test".

But the great thing is the Network doesn't need to have a single positioning, it can serve several niches at once, and expand across more. This is where the app layer comes in handy… These can serve as powerful gateways to the network through _utility_.

And you guys are describing lots of them.

We think there is a powerful proposition for the utility of the network when it comes to personal, private, and secure use of AI. And there's a very compelling reason to do that right now. But it's just one of many ways we can "show, not tell" what it can do.

## Monday, 2024-03-04

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `10:08:36` **jimcollinson** said:

Yeah the token is just a bit of glue (or more like oil, really!) that lets the economy between Creativity and needs on the one side, and resource and solutions on the other.

It's a way to functionally replace what is there at them moment: attention, surveillance, attention, advertising, and hyper-consumerism. 

So it's not _unimportant_ it's just not the main event. Like the oil my car has got to be there, it's critical,  a lot of engineering goes into it, and presumably somewhere there are communities of folk that just love to geek out on engine oil (and that's cool)…

But it's what the car _allows me to do_, and the _destination_ it takes me to, that is the real sizzle.

## Friday, 2024-03-08

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `08:27:02` **jimcollinson** said:

Filecoin is really pretty different. It’s a marketplace for data storage credits. Which you then go and spend with a provider who hosts your data on trad servers, and IPFS points at it. 

Our network actually does all the:

- market 
- economy
- storage (permanent)
- data handling (all quantum secure)

All autonomously. It _is_ one giant global scale server that we all get a slice of. Not just a decentralised market.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1215576500418646126)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `08:32:08` **jimcollinson** said:

> *Replying to jimcollinson:*
> Filecoin is really pretty different. It’s a marketplace for data storage credits. Which you then go ... [truncated]

Crazy thing about filecoin that folk might not realise, is that once you’ve got the token and agreed a price with a provider, you have to contact the directly and arrange between you how to get the data to them. Then after a period, your contract will run out, and you’ll have to pay again or do the whole thing all over.

Not the cloud we envisioned.

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `15:19:51` **jimcollinson** said:

A bit that is easy to miss when it comes to the utility of the token within the network, over a currency external to it is:

- **Security**: it's one of the methods through which good behaviour by nodes on the network is autonomously rewarded and bad behaviour is ignored (stigmergy). 
- **Economy Accessibility**: I can offset my usage costs, by offering my spare resources. I don't need to buy any tokens, or hold any particular currency for this. It can all stay barter on the network if you want. It also makes the network _globally_ accessible and lest reliant on external systems.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1215680393160691712)

It doesn’t use a blockchain, and there are privacy enhancing features, but it’s not a privacy coin, no.

Ok, I wanna help you folks in your quest. No spoilers, but a few reminders of the parameters at play. 

Any name must:

- Not have any trademark conflicts (EU/US/CH) in classes relating to networks, finance, comms, software, AI etc
- Have a useable ticker that hasn’t been taken on any CEX
- Be easy to pronounce/communicate
- No embarrassing translations or connotations 
- Vibes

Easy!

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `19:13:08` **jimcollinson** said:

There are teams already developing social networks that will operate on the safe network. But they will use significantly different business models than the highly algorithmically surveillance-based ad models that support the likes of facebook. And that's by design. The network can't know, nor learn about you from your browsing habits. 

It's built on privacy by design principles.

Could you do advertising on the Network? Sure. But it would be back to traditional billboard-style, or product placement advertising, rather than highly targeted attention economy, click-bait inducing, behavioural modification models that we experience at the moment.

And I think that will be a positive step toward a better Internet.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1216463874157580439)

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `07:55:36` **jimcollinson** said:

We are aiming to reward participants in the Beta. It won't be a _straight_ swap, test-tokens for live-tokens, as we can't do that from a legal perspective. But we are able to use test tokens as a form of measure of involvement, and then rewards accordingly from a dedicated allocation of live-tokens via the foundation. The details are still being finalised, and it will be opt-in not automatic, but it should be fun!

And as you say, the aim is to persist data over from the last of the betas to the live network, so there is great value in participation there too.

## Thursday, 2024-03-14

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `11:14:57` **jimcollinson** said:

There's a route to getting to the "granny proof" product though. And in my opinion, it's not a straight line. We won't be able to get there by just targeting and building for "the granny" because the mindset shift, and behavioural inertia we have to come over is so large.

There are ways to do it though, and pointers to the route needed (and it is something that Maslow would have something to say about).

In fact I made a video on my thoughts about it a while back, if you have the time:

https://youtu.be/5NvZ-NDM6bU?si=6kGkCO_m6GXzD--h

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `19:02:41` **jimcollinson** said:

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `20:36:29` **jimcollinson** said:

As far as the Network itself goes, no.

When it comes to what goes on at the client though—the app itself—then that is in the hands of Proton. But the ability is there to put that all in the hands of the consumer though: there keys their data.

We can now start thinking about apps and services in the same way as we did back in the pre-web days, like when you would install software on a desktop PC, it's just there for you to manipulate your own data—there are no eyeballs on the back end of it.  

Accept instead of all your data sitting on a hard drive on your desk… it's now in the ether, in the massive monolithic array, accessible only to you, but from any device, and will all the connected goodness that the internet can provide.

It can be that way should orgs decide to write it that way.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1217934400814186686)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `20:38:58` **jimcollinson** said:

Obvs, there are always ways to get at things on an individual level should a powerful adversary want to though… like through 'equipment interference' on your local machine. The Network can't protect you from _everything_ …

but it is a massive leap forward (or maybe backward, and then into a new alternative future the cloud never had)

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1217935028269486232)

## Friday, 2024-03-15

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `19:57:34` **jimcollinson** said:

At a macro level, decisions on the operation, evolution, and ongoing health of the Network are in the collective hands of node operators.

Anyone can modify node software, and therefore node behaviour. 

But any modifications to that behaviour either need to improve performance within the collectively accepted norms and expected node behaviour, as understood/seen by other nodes in randomly assigned close groups (and thus the network as a whole) or nodes will face being ignored, ostracised from the Network economy, and punted off the Network.

Soooo… any modded node software, while it can be run by any single node, must involve the overall cooperation and consensus of a large majority of nodes in the Network to change behaviour overall. This is "the forking" of the network.

Plus… Network behaviour is also, in essence, governed by the economics of supply and _demand_, and thus must take into account the needs of people storing data on the Network, and external factors influencing those needs.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1218286994073845860)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `19:58:35` **jimcollinson** said:

It's like an anarchic system of governance or, massive consensus

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1218287251805569054)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `20:00:10` **jimcollinson** said:

So if you want to change the network you either need to own a hugenormous majority of nodes (expensive + hard)…

Or, you form agreement and cooperation from node operators to make the changes in step togther (through trust, and agreement)

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1218287648335069286)

So the answers to resilleince of governace and decentralisation of the systems that keep the thing ticking and strong are diversity of node operators (hence accessibility, small nodes, commodity hardware, low barriers to entry) and good comms, community, and transparency

Not to pish on your bonfire pishing @T… but it's all just data. And the communication alround that data. So if folk wanted to create tokens and token systems on top of the Network, they totally could. There is nothing inherently wrong with it…

But making little economies that can do their own thing, and communities around them? Sure, it can do that. And it brings a bunch of cool possibilities that don't fit in the current blockchain mold either.

## Friday, 2024-03-22

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `13:36:34` **jimcollinson** said:

There's a few things there… speed of a single payment, and how many the network can handle concurrently—which then has a knock-on effect for individual payment performance at busy times—and then how these things scale with network size.

The design of Autonomi means that the bigger it gets, the more it can handle, which is the opposite of most blockchain solutions.

Plus there is also the size of transactions (teeny-tiny), and the lack of fees which should make it very useful for services which want to reward small interactions, such as IoT or DePIN type usecases

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1220727830439006320)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `13:43:55` **jimcollinson** said:

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `07:35:53` **jimcollinson** said:

There is a form of public ledger, yes, but it's not a blockchain… it's represented in a DAG. Anyone can use the ledger to check the validity of a transaction and it's parents (to make sure that it is legit). this is so people can be certain there are no double spends etc. This graph can also be traced right back to genesis (should you want to put the time in) so the whole supply can be verified.

But… you can't go snooping about in people's wallets like you can with blockchain, as they are derived addresses. You can tell which ones are yours, but the general public can't. Unless you choose to tell them.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1222086611504726048)

---

## Wednesday, 2024-05-01

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `08:35:25` **jimcollinson** said:

You may be overthinking it somewhat…

Agreeing to the telemetry is just part of the deal when being in the beta rewards program, it's really a big part of what you are being rewarded for… having useful info and logs sent back to base so we can debug, improve, and get ready for launch. We can gather stuff from beta testers that we can't on the live network, so part of it is for that.

The other part of it is just being rewarded for helping build the capacity and resilience of the Beta, and making swelling in to a big unstoppable network that will become the one we launch!

So we can count up the work that your nodes have done, and also the number of individual contributors, as well as communicate with all participants (and make it fun!) we'll have a Discord ID pinged back to MaidSafe along with your test tokens when your node earns them. That will allow us to run the league tables, and then calculate the real tokens we'll be paying you after launch, to thank you for all the testing!

All the angles we are hitting with our Beta Rewards program, and while assembling THE WORLD BRAIN togeher:

1. Rewarding you all for your time and effort and resources
2. Expanding the capacity of the Network
3. Expanding the reach and user base of the Beta (without hurting 2.)
4. Testing the infra, and getting results back to the mothership (with the absolute minimum privacy worries)
5. Testing the dynamics of the economy as best we can (without gameability)
6. Testing the MAID/eMAID conversion process
7. Making it fun
8. Making it accessible
9. Giving people an avenue for contributing tech and non-tech skills for all the above
10. Making sure its easy to get your earnings after the launch with the most minimal personal data required to do so.

(all within the bounds of our resources)

## Thursday, 2024-05-16

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `15:40:47` **jimcollinson** said:

It's worth remembering though, that there are different needs for different audiences.

Many introductions stay at the big picture, and the vision, and the mid/longterm aims and capabilities of Autonomi… and are pitched at a consumer audience.

But many very rapidly want immediate depth, and comparisons with direct alternatives that are already decentralised, and often have the same aims.

That kind of depth, and comparison to things like blockchain, and other distributed systems, and cryptography etc is absolutely necessary.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1240675322278576158)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `15:54:57` **jimcollinson** said:

Agreed

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1240678888045150310)

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `16:43:12` **jimcollinson** said:

We'll be launching a really cool Beta Network with a full Rewards Program at the start of June.

That'll allow you to contribute your spare computer resource, and then get a slice of a big token pool when the main net launches later in the year.

So stay tuned, as the earlier you get in on that the better.

Oh and we'll multiplying rewards each time we hit key targets for participant numbers… so great to be inviting in your friends to join in the fun too!

Rebuilding the web from the ground up is a team game 💪🏻

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1240691031452946443)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `21:00:17` **jimcollinson** said:

Autonomi, contains a Distributed Ledger Technology. It's a key part of how the economy works.

It may not be a blockchain… but it is still a DLT, both in a technical, practical, and also legal sense.

I get it, that blockchains can sometimes feel like tainted tech. So things that fall under a similar umbrella, that we don't want to be tainted by the same, compel us to attempt to yank it from the underneath. Perhaps reclassify it, with a deft linguistic twist. But that can often be a losing battle; a waste of energy.

I find it much more fruitful to focus on _what it can do_ and how it meets the vision, and perhaps, if necessary, point to how this technology has finally begun living up to the promises.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1240755728273117336)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `21:01:22` **jimcollinson** said:

I mean it is that too… but it also has a DL, which doesn't do _the storage_, but is part of what makes it all function.

## Tuesday, 2024-05-28

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `12:50:12` **jimcollinson** said:

Yeah, for the beta, the amount your nodes will do doesn't translate directly into rewards. It's a competition for a fixed pool of rewards (but one that we'll keep multiplying!)

So think of it like an MMO game. We'll have a leaderboard, and the player with the most points at the end of the beta will get the biggest prize, but there will be prizes all the way down the scoreboard.

Plus:

- The sooner you are involved, the fewer people you'll be competing with
- We'll also be rewarding people for helping getting others involved
- The more people involved, the more rewards will multiply for everyone.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1244981047288922112)

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `11:11:24` **jimcollinson** said:

We need to:

- Build Network capacity and size
- Test the Network in a range of scenarios, and use cases, taking into account a variety of hardware, and human behaviours
- Get as close to real dynamics of the economy as we can, while not launching the real tradable token
- Get more reach, and build the community
- Encourage people to refer and bring in more node ops, while not creating a perverse incentive to do so
- Do all of the above in a _somewhat_ controlled manner so we can build a resilient base

It's a tall order to do all this at once, but we think we have found a way to do it. It's not going to be perfect… but it should be fun! And won't it be nice to actaully be able to reward people for their efforts after all this time?

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1247492900724543498)

**[#🎫︱general-support]** `13:18:03` **jimcollinson** said:

# The Beta is Now Live!

## Time to start some nodes

1. Open the [Node Launchpad](https://docs.autonomi.com/getting-started/autonomi-beta/downloads)
2. [Reset it](https://docs.autonomi.com/getting-started/autonomi-beta/quickstart-guide/resetting-your-nodes) (if you haven't done so already)
3. Add your Discord Username by using [Ctrl + B]
4. Add some Nodes and get started with [Ctrl +G].
5. You are underway! It can take a few minutes for your nodes to connect.
6. Check your progress using the [Discord Bot](https://docs.autonomi.com/getting-started/beta-rewards-program/using-the-discord-bot). If you're in the Beta Reward Program you'll see your place on the leaderboard as soon as your first Nanos land.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1247881515107483759/1247887159990685747)

**[#🎫︱general-support]** `20:34:04` **jimcollinson** said:

Just a wee update on the Bot reporting situation…

The wee fella is taking it time isn't it?  On slow mode at the moment… and counting nanos from from the DAG at abacus speed. Slower than is ideal! 

The rapid expansion of the Network meant that it's been chasing his tail from the start;  we should have set him loose on turbo mode to stay up to keep pace from the off, but we are working on a fix which should give him a caffeine shot tomorrow.

Rest assured though, that all your nanos are being logged, and stored on the DAG. That's the tree-like structure that keeps a note of _every_ transaction that happens on the Network. The bot just audits them, and then spits them out here when he gets to each one.

If you see a total of Nanos in the launchpad, then they are logged! Fix incoming as soon as we can so you can get that info from the bot, and see you leaderboard position.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1247881515107483759/1247996885755756624)

## Tuesday, 2024-06-18

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `15:10:11` **jimcollinson** said:

# We've Improved the Bot Reporting Again
===========

We've updated and upgraded the DAG (the graph of transactions the Network generates, and from where the Bot gets its information) again, so if you hit `/rank` you should get the most up-to-date information

The update should also speed up the Bot a bit more too!

Please go ahead and hit the `/rank` command and give the Bot a little nudge and a refresh for us.


# Launchpad Nano Total Bug — Fix incoming
===========

We've tracked down a bug that can mean an inconsistency between the Launchpad Nano total and what the Bot reports. 

In short, the Launchpad sometimes attempts to send in the same earnings twice. This, rightly, gets knocked back by the Network—so it's not reported by the Bot—but the Launchpad adds it to the total, leading them to be slightly out of sync. It's the DAG, and therefore the Bot, that shows the correct total: the source of truth.

We've got a fix incoming for that, and it'll be sorted in the next release.


# We're Increasing Uploads Some More
===========

We're still keeping it steady while we gather data and improve, but we're ramping up data uploads once again. Doubling the rate in fact, so you should see more Nanos coming your way.

We're also wrapping up a Network-wide upgrade at the moment which aims to massively improve performance, and resilience, overall. That's going into internal testing as we speak… landing with your as soon as we've put it through its paces!

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1252626423248850974)

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `08:08:43` **jimcollinson** said:

One point of comparison with ICP, relevant to our Beta is what is needed to run a node and contribute.

For ICP you need a data centre, $300k capital, and a data compliance officer.

That's right, the interesting thing is that the "decentralized" centralized projects like Filecoin are finding ways to include the common man, which is good.  For example, I found out about this today and I'm testing it on my autonomi nodes machine https://www.filstation.app/

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1255782903242297431)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `08:19:51` **jimcollinson** said:

All of this stuff is cool, and I'm for it. 

But do remember: the Filecoin Network doesn't do any storage. It's just a decentalised marketplace for storage providers to make sales for their storage.

The stack/process is: 

- IPFS makes the data addresses (pointers to data)
- Filecoin creates the _market_ for the data providers
- Users send data to the provider directly (and encrypt it themselves if they want it private). Sometimes even arranging this by email shipping drives if needed!
- Storage providers then hold that data in a traditional way on a contractual basis

But with Autonomi the _Network itself_ does:

- Addressing
- Encryption
- Decentralised/autonomous market/economy
- Permanent Storage
- Payments

The whole lot. And all on everyday machines.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1255784650354458634)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `08:29:43` **jimcollinson** said:

All data stored on the nodes is in encrypted chunks that can't be reconstructed. So there is no way for you, or software on your PC, to make any use of it.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1255787132715405342)

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `08:33:20` **jimcollinson** said:

All the chunks are totally random as well, evenly distributed across the globe. Plus they get shuffled between nodes all the time. So the chances of you even having a complete file (even if you could decrypt it, which you can't) are practically zero.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1255788040194887700)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `09:06:04` **Deleted User** replied to jimcollinson:

> *jimcollinson said:*
> All data stored on the nodes is in encrypted chunks that can't be reconstructed. So there is no way ... [truncated]

Data isn't necessarily encrypted. If you use the Autonomi apps and the relevant APIs it will be, but there's nothing to force a chunk to be encrypted. In fact, the current APIs make it hard to do this for data in memory. The self encryption crate only supports encryption of files, so if you have data in memory you can't use self encryption directly or are forced to write it to disk. Writing data to local disk is not a good thing unless it is necessary, so devs either do that to use self encryption, figure out their own encryption scheme (good luck with that for public data) or quite likely store some chunks unencrypted.

It makes it hard for developers to do the right thing. I've raised this from time to time, again this week where Gabriel is looking at the self encryption crate but I don't know if it has been noted or likey to be addressed.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1255796279557226619)

---

The network is blocking under-performing nodes more readily now, and you may have some zombie nodes that have not made the cut

## Saturday, 2024-08-10

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `08:57:01` **jimcollinson** said:

Global network, with different laws in a bazillion different jurisdictions, and of course IANAL, this it not legal advice etc…

But the data on nodes isn't content; nor is it information. Nor can it be reassembled by a node operator even if they wanted to. It's just random 1s and 0s.

And we are adding in another layer before launch which further encrypts the already encrypted data store on device… so you can;t even see those chunks.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1271739065775165554)

But laws when it comes to decentrlaised networks lag very far behind; and existing laws don't really even adequately describe things in relation to decentralised networks… it's all very client-server and customer/provider/data-controller… which tends towards a grey untested mush

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `10:15:02` **happybeing** replied to jimcollinson:

> *jimcollinson said:*
> Global network, with different laws in a bazillion different jurisdictions, and of course IANAL, thi... [truncated]

> But the data on nodes isn't content; nor is it information. Nor can it be reassembled by a node operator even if they wanted to. It's just random 1s and 0s.

I keep seeing this being said and I have been pointing out privately that it isn't currently the case. At the moment not all data is encrypted on the hard drives of nodes - just search a few of your node records/chunks for certain strings linke "index.html". I know you plan to add a layer of encryption on top which is great - and important because of this issue. But that doesn't make the statement that all records *are* encrypted true. Until then I think it is important not to say that.

## Wednesday, 2024-08-14

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `12:37:36` **jimcollinson** said:

Yeah, this was the original approach we took, but it quickly becomes very complex, and actually delivering a worse UX. There are just too many variables, and it's difficult to take into account some of the softer metrics such as individual use patterns.

In the end, the solution (for improved UX, without a huge build) is to give finer grained and progressive controls back to the user, and letter them tune things to suit. Specifically by allowing them to add and remove nodes one at, and giving feedback on the resource useage and health of each

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1273244131262726195)

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `19:28:41` **jimcollinson** said:

I don't believe data should have an expiry date for a number of reasons… one of them being the [subject of my video](https://x.com/WithAutonomi/status/1823748473633571104) today. Another being that we don't know what data will be valuble in the future.

But there are a number of factors that allow perpetual data:

- Moore/Kryder's Law
- Deduplication at a chunk level
- Ever-improving compression
- Longer term: Archive nodes as required

Those are the bullet points, I should probably do a video on it though!

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1273347585268125769)

Even that's not quite right… More nodes — and the potential for more nodes across more machines as facilitated by smaller nodes — means more even spread of data, and less likelyhood of chunks for a single file being contained within a single area, or with a single node operator.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1278356275004182591)

**[#🎫︱general-support]** `11:08:59` **jimcollinson** said:

We are talking probabilities though. 

The probability of data loss occurring with 5 nodes out of 1000 in a full network is small. The more you turn off, the higher the probability.

The number of nodes you'd have to turn of to _guarantee_ data loss is 800/1000.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1247881515107483759/1283006302313779222)

---

**[#🎫︱general-support]** `11:09:34` **jimcollinson** said:

And of course, things are more tolerant the _less full_ the network gets as the data gets replicated and moved to other nodes when they come and go

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1247881515107483759/1283006448233742401)

Yes, that's correct, the native token is in the network at the moment; but that's not all that is required for a functioning network economy ready for launch. We need _integration_ with the outside world to allow the flow of value (and data) into the Network.

It also requires confidence on the part or 3rd parties to integrate; and that takes time (and money).

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `15:15:30` **jimcollinson** said:

To port forward:

- Go to options (`O`)
- Press `Ctrl+K` and change the connection mode to Custom Ports
- Set the start of the range of 50 ports (I'd recommend starting at 50000)
- Then you'll need to go to your router admin and set up port-forwarding to your device for that range of ports (`50000-50049` in this example, internal and external ports the same is what I do)
- I'd also recommend having a firewall enabled when you are doing this as well

Let us know how you get on!

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1283430726452248636)

- Disaster recovery
- Wallets

- Accelerated path to the native token
- A functioning usable live network in a matter of months

But going for a big bang all or nothing yeet into a native token, we do not get these things

## Sunday, 2024-09-15

**[#🎫︱general-support]** `08:34:12` **jimcollinson** said:

1. You can, it's up to you. You'll be able to (after a bit of a wait sometimes) see all your earnings here, using the `rank` command if you do. If you don't want to, then you're nanos will jiust be stored locally, and not immediatly sent back to base. It's not all or nothing either, when using the Node Manager, it just on a node by node basis. use the `--owner flag` when starting a node.

2.
   - As above, set the `--owner` flag on each node you start to add your discord name. Or leave it off if you want to keep the nanos
- The launchpad app is just a terminal UI on top of the node manager. And the nodes are just services that run in the background started by either
- You can use both! Id say just state the lauchpad to see how it suits you, and if you need a bit more control that the UI allows, fire up the node manager
- Yup!

3. Yes, you'll need to make sure a firewall isn't blocking the `safenode` services that fire up. You can add an exception.

I'd say quickest/easiest way to get going is the launchpad… give that a bash. But it's all the same under the hood.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1247881515107483759/1284779290101288960)

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `18:06:57` **jimcollinson** said:

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `18:25:17` **jimcollinson** said:

> *Will there be any mechanism to enforce having 32(5)GB available space per node?*

There is no meaningful way to _enforce_ having a specific amount of space available on a node. The 32GB size means "this is the maxium number of records the network expects you to keep without being shunned". It's a cap. 

If you under-provision and then can't store when asked, you get shunned. That's the network working as designed.

> *Have internal test filled up any of the 32GB nodes?*

I'm not conducting the tests, and TBH my brain hurt looking at the designs, but I'm hearing a readout of the results. And 32GB is the leader at the moment, and unless the continuing tests over the weekend say otherwise, we'll be going with 32GB on Tuesday.

> *When you say it has performed best, what was it up against and what criteria were used to declare 32GB was best?*

2, 4, 8, 16 and 32GB, all at a variety of chunk sizes, fullness, churn, and download rates. Observing: mem, cpu, network traffic, libp2p error rate, libp2p success rate, parallel download rate, upload rate.

> *Does this mean we may see a test of 64Gb nodes?*

No. Becuase we may be into only marginal gains there… but the main effect would be cutting off smaller devices and the potential for mobile nodes down the line.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1291813409075236934)

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `12:12:32` **aceweb1978** replied to jimcollinson:

> *jimcollinson said:*
> Yeah, your OS will just see it as a single drive, so you should be good to go

That's what the technical service of the server rental replied to me::

"Yes, in this case, it is RAID 0.

However, we note that in RAID 0, data is written to the disks in a fragmented manner, i.e., a file can be split across two disks.

Such systems increase the write speed to the virtual disk that is created when setting up the RAID, but in the event of one of the physical disks failing, all data written to both disks is lost.

You can create such a RAID if losing data is not critical for you.

You can create a RAID during system reinstallation in our control panel, in which case all data on the disks will be deleted.

If you need this solution as a replacement for one disk that you previously requested, then in this case, we recommend waiting for our colleagues' response on Monday and possibly ordering a new server with one disk, since the failure rate of RAID 0 is higher than that of a single disk of the required volume."

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1292081992762130432)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `12:18:27` **jimcollinson** said:

The thing is, in your case, Raid0 is fine really. In the case that a drive did fail, there are 4 other copies of the data on the network. So really all it means is your nodes can’t earn for the time it takes you to swap out the disk and get the back online.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1292083481211568150)

## Thursday, 2024-10-10

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `13:09:41` **jimcollinson** said:

This is how we are thinking about Autonmous Networks, from our 2010 White Paper: https://docs.maidsafe.net/Whitepapers/pdf/AutonomousNetwork.pdf

> "Autonomous networks are self-healing, selfmanaging and most importantly independent of human interference. Such networks will be able to be developed in a way that avoids wasting effort on maintaining even simple mechanisms such as storage, scalability and data retention."

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1293908313175752844)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `13:13:26` **jimcollinson** said:

You can have a decentralised network that's not autonomous, but not the other way around.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1293909255933395036)

If you mean a _[one time fee](https://docs.autonomi.com/learn/introduction/what-is-autonomi/lifetime-storage-one-time-fee)_ to upload a file — then _yes_ ✅

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `11:51:39` **jimcollinson** said:

Each node randomly gets the value of CPU, and if over 50% will turn itself off.  Each node is on a slightly different interval + random seconds , so not all will shutdown when 50% strikes. There are 3 measurements , 1 minute apart, and they all have to be > 50% for it to decide to turn off.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1299324494929858560)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `11:52:16` **jimcollinson** said:

But, nodes won't restart themselves. You have to do that.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1299324646952275978)

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `14:18:13` **jimcollinson** said:

Okay okay okay…

**Launchpad Users**

What would you say to us about replacing the `Attos Earned` display at the top with your `Wallet Balance`

Reason I'm testing the water with this one is to make it immediately more useful, because:

- Currently, it shows attos earned in the _session_ so can go down or go to zero when you are resetting/restarting things
- It's currently quite tricky to see your attos in most wallets, including metamask
- You'd still be able to keep track of attos hitting it from nodes… even though there may be a slight delay depending on implementation. But not Bot (rest his soil) level delays.


What say ye? Good? Bad?  Something I'm missing?

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `14:11:19` **heyjon_55** replied to jimcollinson:

> *jimcollinson said:*
> Yes, as Dimitar says, this is only the start of the early launch phase, there is much more to come, ... [truncated]

What is emissions?

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1301549067914186845)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `14:35:11` **jimcollinson** said:

Not quite…

The number of tokens earned by node operators from data payments is governed by factors including: the amount of data uploaded, network size, and the fullness of the node storage.

Emissions is the Network effectivly distributing _additional_ supply of tokens on top of those circulating in the market for data payments. So how many new tokens get added in, to support the node operators overall. 

Later on in this early phase of launch, these emissions will be turned on, and more tokens will be entering the economy, and make their way to node operators to support thier operation.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1301555073821708299)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `14:37:38` **jimcollinson** said:

Also kicking myself for dropping an acronym there without explanation.  

But yeah, it's the Token Generation Event where the live supply of tokens will be created and be traceable… coinciding with the full public launch of the network completing, and the real fun beginning!

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1301555689545797662)

## Friday, 2024-11-22

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `15:42:37` **jimcollinson** said:

This concept, along with the Network Roalyties system that would have underpinned them, have been shelved for the foreseeable future — likely permanently.

I know it's loss to many, but to others a win — there was the perception of them as a tax.

But overall, it simplifies the tokenomics, and operation of the Network a great deal, so allows us to launch faster, and start benefiting the world.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1309544577392316487)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `15:43:47` **jimcollinson** said:

There is, however, going to be a builders rewards program which will be similar to Network Royalties in many ways — but just from a fixed foundation pool, which will likely last around 5-10 years.

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `10:11:54` **janeytheterrible** replied to jimcollinson:

> *jimcollinson said:*
> Are you, and anyone else experiencing such things with Hertzner, able to forward me the corresponden... [truncated]

While this is important to do and very much needed.  It does highlight the need to only have a small %age of nodes on any data centre provider's infrastructure.  The reason this has occurred is that with such a high %age of nodes on Hetzner that any one home node setup of any size are contacting so many nodes on so many VPS that hetzner IDS has seen it as that home connect scanning their VPS on a large scale.  Reduce the %age of network nodes on hetzner and you reduce dramatically this apparent abusive behaviour.  You cannot expect every provider to incorporate special conditions just for Autonomi that might then allow attackers a way to attack

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1317071495587168336)

One thing I think might be of importance for Autonomi is that it might need more copies than centralized options.

## Wednesday, 2025-01-08

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `17:40:55` **jimcollinson** said:

Remember what I was saying last night about the timing of the Network launch being so perfect, so needed?

https://www.forbes.com/sites/aldenabbott/2025/01/03/net-neutrality-rule-goes-down-other-regs-may-follow/

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1326606579981877249)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `17:41:54` **jimcollinson** said:

If the courts won't guarantee Net Neutrality, I guess we're gonna have to have encryption do it.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1326606824543092930)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `17:56:50` **jimcollinson** said:

If Net Neutrality isn't enforced by the courts, ISPs can look at your traffic and decide to throttle it based on what it is. Many such example of this… ISPs slowing down certain streaming services to inflate the performance of their own rival system for example.

Or Facebook get's a fastlane, where your blog, or challenger platform is down some pegs.

With a network like Autonomi — everything is self-encypted and all data just looks the same. It's all noise. So one type of data cannot be prioritised over another: a level, neutral playingfield by default.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1326610584199761932)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `18:02:26` **musik1976** replied to jimcollinson:

> *jimcollinson said:*
> If Net Neutrality isn't enforced by the courts, ISPs can look at your traffic and decide to throttle... [truncated]

Thank you for explaining.  In terms of the last paragraph.  From following the forum this is what I had understood.  All data looks the same but, why then were there issues with, i think it was hefner?, concerning the vps's, they noticed something different, or is this a separate issue?

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1326611994303791104)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `18:04:14` **jimcollinson** said:

That's a separate thing. What we are talking about here is you the end user of the Internet, and your ISP deciding that some of the apps our sites you use should be slower than others.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1326612445942255688)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `18:05:19` **jimcollinson** said:

But what we are talking about here is baking it into the Internet at a structural level, rather than pushing it onto the end consumer to find (and pay for) a workaround.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1326612718102384782)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `18:16:11` **jimcollinson** said:

But from a business/publisher/app perspective, it still requires a consumer-side adoption and action… it's a consumer solution. Whereas if we can imagine a world where all traffic and comms are e2ee by default, at a network level, then it's a done deal for both parties.

Either way, we are both still arguing that encryption is the answer 😉

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1326615453958803497)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `23:53:44` **janeytheterrible** replied to jimcollinson:

> *jimcollinson said:*
> If Net Neutrality isn't enforced by the courts, ISPs can look at your traffic and decide to throttle... [truncated]

Not just throttle but they can insert adverts, outright block access to competitors to their ISP business.  OR even take payments from a car manufacturer to block any advert or web page displaying anther car company's info.

It truly becomes a wild west where the ISP can gatekeep anything, even break encryption by forcing you to use their certificates.  IE force you to enable browsers to accept their certificates or make the browser supplier do it

## Monday, 2025-01-13

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `08:25:13` **jimcollinson** said:

Dave is an example app to get people started uploading/downloading private data to the Network without needing to use a command line interface. So it's a 'client' app.

Nodes will still be operated with the Launchpad and Node Manager / command line. But other developers are already working on other ways to run nodes (even dedicated hardware) and we can anticipate some will start incorporating nodes within client apps, so people can have all-in-one type expereinces.

APIs and SDKs being published soon will really accellrate all this. So much fun about to happen!

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `15:01:45` **jimcollinson** said:

But generally, we are considering a data network as autonomous if it does _all_ of the following:

- Data Storage itself
- Creates the market for that data
- Dynamic pricing for the above
- Secures and serves this data
- Does this all without human intervention

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1329465625759973378)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `15:02:30` **jimcollinson** said:

It's basically a way of differentiating from decentralised networks that only really do a portion of this job

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `20:53:53` **jimcollinson** said:

From _the man himself_

> Self encryption does this
>
>→ chunk file
>**→ Compress chunk**
>→ take hash
>→ use the next chunk hash to encrypt the next chunk
>→ Use previous 2 hashes and XOR the next chunk
>→ Hash content and make this hash the name of the chunk

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1329916632188846201)

First raw capacity is how much potential DATA you can store.  What you call RAW is the Diskspace used to provide that RAW capacity.  The 5 minimum copies has to be applied to get potential storage available.

Trying to inflate things to appear better is only going to bite you in the butt with people turning away (silently) ignoring Autonomi as a scam inflating things and these people turning away are potential uploaders looking for storage solutions for their TB/PB data systems.

The real figures for raw storage capacity of 1.1 PB in the tiny network is terrific, no need for inflation

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `10:06:55` **jimcollinson** said:

It very much depends on the angle you choose to look at from. I always quote this number alongside the number of Nodes, looking at it from the perspective of what capacity is being offered _to_ the network. 

I.e. currently

**198,000 nodes are providing 6 PiB of capacity _to_ the Network. ** (Raw Capacity) — the power of what collectively people are all banding together to provide for all the goodness that the network can provide. How much spare space from old PCs, and on desktops, and dusty corners of data centres is being pledged in order to secure user data and make it accessible, redundant, etc.

*This then means that… *

**The Network can provide 1.2 PiB of data storage *to* Users** and with this, it's redundantly stored, perpetual (after TGE ofc!), enctypted, globally accessible etc etc.

**[#🎙︱discussion-topics]** `21:22:38` **jimcollinson** said:

Simple explanation is: All the nodes work away, and if they behave well in storing  and serving network data, then eventually they will be selected to receive a new bit of data, which they get paid for. So over time they all should end up earning some thing. 

Attos are tiny fractions of a whole token, so you may recieve many of them depending on a number of factors, including supply/demand for storage on the network at any given time.

Yes and no. It really depends on the nature of the data, and how utilise the data types available via the API. Some of them you could think of as blobs that are just overwritten entirely, others like a list you are just making an edit to, but the history is maintained.

But remember there are other pricing factors in play here when making the comparison. e.g.

- There are no charges to download the data after it's stored
- No egress fees
- Etc.

# Preview of TGE and documentation including MaidSafeCoin conversion process — call for Questions an feedback

Bit of a pre-announcement announcement here but I wanted to give you a preview of the documentation relating to TGE, and, importantly the [MaidSafeCoin conversion process](https://docs.autonomi.com/ant-token/converting-maidsafecoin/process-overview).

We are keen to get any questions (so we can fill in any gaps and FAQs) along with feedback as we firm things up for tomorrow.

Here are the latest docs covering all things [Ant Token](https://docs.autonomi.com/ant-token) plus an updated and slimmed down [Node section](https://docs.autonomi.com/node/nodes-post-tge) catering for the post-TGE world.

A few notable omissions are on their way, and will be slotted in as soon as we've type them up:

- The on-the-day process for updating Nodes
- How emissions work nodes after TGE
- Specific date and times for BitMart conversion
- The Token contract address to use when importing ANT to your wallet
- Process for redeeming Beta Rewards from a Discord Username


So a few more pieces to slot in, but we felt it important to get the MaidSafeCoin conversion guide in front of you in particular. 

Please do give us your comments and questions!

## Monday, 2025-02-17

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `11:41:59` **jimcollinson** said:

Getting them the files is interesting as well. In some circumstances, it's literally "ship me a hard drive". 

So not really an apples-apples comparison

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1341011763256365137)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `14:44:34` **jimcollinson** said:

Filecoin doesn;t really store anything. It's a market place _for_ storage. So you buy filecoin, wrap up your data in IPFS, and then negotiate for storage direct with a provider… and get them the data in a way that is mutually agreed — then you have to keep on paying them if you want the data to stay up.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1341057713962225725)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `14:45:59` **jimcollinson** said:

So, it's still cool that it is using decentralised tech — IPFS (decentrlaised addresses for data, and a way to structure it — pointers to data), and Filecoin, a decentralised marketplace for people who want to use IPFS. But no actually storage of the data

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1341058069345603606)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `14:47:43` **jimcollinson** said:

Whereas Autonomi does:

- The addressing bit (similar to the way IPFS works)
- The market place for data storage — dynamic supply and demand from nodes (replacing filecoin)
- _And_ the network itself actually stores the data as well
- (plus it's all encrypted)

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1341058507423879260)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `14:51:16` **jimcollinson** said:

Oh and another thing… as IPFS is just pointers to data… you might have yourself a nice digital asset, that you think you own, becuase you have the unique IPFS address to it, and that's yours. But one day, you have a look for the data that lives at that address… and booof! It' gone!

Because it needs ongoing hosting somewhere, and needs to be "pinned" to be always available. And someone has to pay for that on an ongoing basis.

So there is no perpetual data.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1341059397551656970)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `15:05:20` **jimcollinson** said:

IPFS is just content addresses. Pointers _to_ data. Not the data itself.

So, if all the hosts of that data go offline, and drop it, then it's gone.

The actaully hosting of IPFS data, on the whole, is just quite traditional cloud like hosting. A lot of it on AWS. There is no automation of replicas etc. It's all up to you to go and find people to host your data, and keep paying them etc.

It's almost like you'd want some sort of autonomous solution for data storage that would take care of all of that stuff for you, isn't it? 😉

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1341062937820925995)

---

> IPFS is just content addresses. Pointers _to_ data. Not the data itself.

So, if all the hosts of th... [truncated]

## Monday, 2025-04-28

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `13:11:23` **jimcollinson** said:

Hi All!

I've pulled together a bit of an FAQ for the Impossible Futures voting phase, which I hope will clarify a few things. If there are any further questions please do ask away!

### Q: How many Phases are there to Impossible Futures?
There are 4 phases.

1. **Voting:** This decides the 12 apps that go through the next phase. The finalists. This is decided entirely by the community.
2. **Backing:** This is where the community can back projects by locking up ANT for 12 months, and get a share of a 1.5 Million ANT pool if they successfully deploy. It also helps determine which apps win the grand prizes, of which the backers get a share too.
3. **Deploying**: This is where the app builders complete and deploy their apps onto the live network. If they successfully deploy, the backers will get their share of the pool, and the app will be in the running for the grand prizes
4. **Adjudication:** This is the final phase to where a panel of judges determine, in part, the grand prizes winners. The prize winners will be determined based on two main factors:
    - 60% weighted based on the _amount_ of backing the app garners, and the _number of unique backers_
    - 40% weighted on subjective criteria determined by they judging panel

### Q: How much does it cost to vote?
Each vote always costs less than 1 ANT. The exact price is determined dynamically based on how many votes an app had in comparison to others. More popular apps will cost more to vote for than less popular apps, but always less that 1 ANT

### Q: Do I get anything for voting?
If you voted for an app that successfully makes it through to the final 12, then you get 1 ANT per vote you cast.

### Q: Do I get anything back if I vote for an app that isn't in the top 12?
No, you don't get your vote cost back.

### Q: Is there a judging aspect to Phase 1, or is it 100% down to voting
Phase 1, which determines the final 12, is all down to voting. There is no judging panel during this phase, judging is just for the last phase to help determine the grand prize winners.

### Q: How many times can I vote?
You can vote as many times as you like, for as many of the projects as you like.

### Q: I'm one of the builders, can vote for my own project?
Sure!

### Q: What's to stop someone waiting until the very last minute and casting lots of votes for a project?
This could happen, but we've built in a mechanism that ramps up the cost of all votes as voting concludes. This is to both encourage you to get stuck in and vote early, and also to reduce and limit the variability towards the end. It would also make it much more costly to jump in at the last minute and cast lots of votes in an attempt to game things.

### Q: So who should you vote for?
We encourage you to vote for projects you genuinely believe in—consider their potential contribution to the ecosystem, their societal impact, feasibility, and the strength of the team behind them.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1366386313254666261)

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `16:14:05` **jimcollinson** said:

> Is there a maximum number of tokens you will refund for voting? If someone puts in 1 million ant to vote for a specific project will they get it back?

Just to be clear… you don't get the ANT back that you vote with. It's a purchase. It's simply that you get 1 ANT per vote you cast, should that app go through to the final 12. So 1 million ANT would get you more than 1 million votes, but would also affect the price.

But, to answer your question, no, there is no limit to how many votes you can cast.

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `17:52:54` **jimcollinson** said:

I think the thought process behind it could be summarised as creating a model that gives:

**Built-in Security:** So mass-bot tactics are expensive and impractical, so you know results come from real voters.
**A stronger turnout**: Because it aims to widen appeal, adds some excitement, and gives something back for people having…
**Skin in the Game**: Because you’re not just clicking a button; you’re investing attention, belief, and a little risk. Along with…
**A Stronger Ecosystem:** Because, a little risk filters out weak ideas early, so the overall network grows with real builders and real believers.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1366457158165725325)

## Thursday, 2025-05-15

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `10:48:53` **jimcollinson** said:

Well, there's lots going on in that thread, but much of the interpretation there was based on a metric for popularity, which was not part of the criteria set out in the T&Cs. We couldn't post-hoc change that criteria, or overlay a popularity metric over the top in the same way, as had this been set out prior, it would have likely changed voting patterns a lot. 

In the end, there was only one project that had a low number of unique voters, and one voter with a 68% share of that vote. None of the rest was clear cut. 

If you want follow-up discussion, let's do so in the forum, as it's easier to follow along.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1374322984411467796)

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `11:23:16` **jimcollinson** said:

At the moment, if you locked 1 ANT, that would get you 1.998 pledge points that you can pledge to an app.

If that app deploys, then you'll be in for a share of the rewards pool, which is split amongst all backers of successful apps, proportional to how much they backed.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1374331639412555830)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `11:24:16` **jimcollinson** said:

On top of that, if the app you backed is a prize winner, you get a split of a USDC cash prize; again split proportionally to how many pledge points you backed.

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `14:49:07` **jimcollinson** said:

Actually, that's even easier.

If you look at the leaderboard, you'll see total pledge points, your pledge points, and then your current split of the reward pool.

Now bear in mind, this is as if _all_ the projects deployed successfully. We hope they all will of course, but if some don't, and you backed ones that did, it means that total would be larger!

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1374383443009343508)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `15:35:50` **jimcollinson** said:

Take this basic example:

Rewards Pool = 50,000 ANT
Total Pledge Points = 600,000
Your Pledged Points = 90,000
Your % of pool = 15%
If all projects deployed, you'd get = **7500 ANT** along with your 90,000 ANT unlocked on 13 June 2026.

Make sense?

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1374395198775230605)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `15:40:10` **jimcollinson** said:

A further example.

Let's say the above is true, but you pledged all your 90,000 on one app, and that turned out to be the only one to deploy.

And there is a total of 100,000 points pledged against that one app. Your 90k plus another 10k from others.

You'd have 90% of the pool.

So **45,000 ANT** rewards. Plus probably some decent cash prizes too, if you pledged that backing during the first week!

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1374396290011631767)

## Tuesday, 2025-06-03

**[#🐛︱bug-reports]** `12:44:16` **jimcollinson** said:

Just had a good ol' discussion about this. Really the docs should say 256 _or_ 128. In the end it doesn't really matter to much at all to the level of security or encryption we end up with… because that part isn't really doing the encryption, more the randomisation. Either 256, or 128, and you still end up with an effective one-time pad / information-theoretically secure system.

- and more!

I agree that a much improved mail system will emerge, but remember that mail has gone through millennia of innovation and email was also an evolution of people trying to improve on the simple concept of mail/letters.

I do think the mail concept that has been evolving for 1000's of years  will stand the test of time, and the mail system for Autonomi will be able to improve on email but fundamentally will not change the concept of mail.  Many have tried over the last 100's of years and have fallen by the wayside.  email came out of early attempts in the 60's to have messages across ARPANET and by about 1970 or 71 email was basically in place.  So even after 50 years people have not been able to make significant changes and survive.  

The era of short messages will remain since that is like passing notes.  And that was the best alternative that has survived because at first phones could not do long messages and passing notes is a long held tradition of the youth, (school anyone) and most others.

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `15:33:11` **mckissick** replied to jimcollinson:

> Sure! Right here, or maybe over on the forum if it is longer form perhaps.

What ideas do you have?

Thanks @JimCollinson for suggesting this.  I did post about the "New Money System for the Future - IOUBI" in the "Related Projects" forum and got a couple comments.

But I think there could be a much bigger offering to people with more tools working together.  Having a perfected, decentralized money to offer would attract tons of users but imagine if it solved other things really well too.

The addons I propose included with the monetary system, could help people solve governance, taxes, advertising, insurance, UBI, greed, crime, data privacy and more.  When added to the advancement we're on track for (aside from computer based solutions), we seem ready to get a whole host of the new future very soon.  To give a preview, imagine lots of things becoming abundant.  By abundant, I mean that we'll have as much as we realistically want, available for near zero marginal cost.  Things like energy, transportation, food diversity/supply, information, privacy, housing, land, virtually everything to run the 99% expected parts of society.  Unfortunately, I don't see everyone getting their own free yacht and helicopter fleet.  But the rest, that's all definitely well in progress.  The only roadblock is most of those technologies need a ubiquitous currency with no centralized or functional problems, a singular interface to 'the net', and a few other things - all that Autonomi is posed to provide.

Let's discuss

## Monday, 2025-10-27

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `11:04:12` **jimcollinson** said:

Paymasters is really a tool, part of a tool kit, that we  give to developers that offer lots of flexibility as to how their apps can work for end users.

- At its most basic: it can allow someone else to fund the gas for the end user
- Or it can allow the user to only hold ant and pay for both with that
- Taking it further the app developer could cover both and have that sorted for the end user and then charge them any which way they like (subscription, one-time fee, promotions, credit card payments etc)
- but all the while the user still is the one in charge of their data.

 The roadmap items for credit card payments, or agentic payments, are separate things again; but all aim to offer options to developers and remove friction for end users.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1432323997122560071)

---

 I think data wallet is actually a fairly useful and elegant term (not sure of the use of "agentic wallets" at this point though!)

**[#🎙︱discussion-topics]** `17:19:34` **mightyfool0689** replied to jimcollinson:

> *jimcollinson said:*
> others can pile in for the deep analysis, I suppose, but remembering the nodes won't just dramatical... [truncated]

This is still one thing that I’m not sure about. I do think the nodes will fill up drastically, because node operators are heavily overprovisioning at the moment. Meaning that once the network starts to fill (even if slowly) there will come a point where node operators will have to scale down their nodes to be able to deliver the storage space required, triggering an event of other nodes filling up more and triggering another wave of scaling down. 

I’m expecting to see this as early as 1,5% node capacity used.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1315677640581054464/1435317565001039883)

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `17:00:35` **jimcollinson** said:

I'll try and answer what I think you're asking! Again, I'm not the expert here, that would be Lajos… hopefully he can jump in and correct me if I'm wrong.

When someone initiates a gasless transaction in dave, 

- The PM the cost of the gas in ETH and gets the exchange rate from an oracle
- that is calculated how much Ant is needed to cover it
- and then this gets returned to the client/lib

 so what comes back with the quote is the estimated ANT for the full shebang. And then the PM takes the max fee, and then refund anything that's excess after the transaction goes through. So there's a refund of any unused portion to the mark account, with only the real amount of ANT deducted.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1436037562308497519)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `17:00:58` **jimcollinson** said:

Wood not made this into a library yet, but we will do! First thing is to show that it works for dave, which will be able to try out in a few minutes!

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1436037661877080208)

## Friday, 2025-11-14

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `16:33:01` **jimcollinson** said:

But then the cascade failure modes of a swing between demand positive to data drought, which we talked about at the time, repeatedly modelled and tested, and then addressed through the whitepaper, haven't been addressed though the advocates of an emission free network. Nor the reality of a cold start.

But we _can_ address things through an inflow of data in both cases… which is what we are all focused on of course!

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1438929727564939335)

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `20:11:28` **davidmc0** replied to jimcollinson:

> *jimcollinson said:*
> But then the cascade failure modes of a swing between demand positive to data drought, which we talk... [truncated]

"But we can address things through an inflow of data in both cases… which is what we are all focused on of course!"

Absolutely; getting inflow of data through demand is primary. It's also good to hear about the other issues you have considered and modelled.

"cascade failure modes of a swing between demand positive to data drought". 

This is one I questioned recently here: https://forum.autonomi.community/t/nov-4-update-from-bux/42556/114?u=davidmc0 and have discussed it at other times as well.

...my question is whether a 'data drought' is realistic once demand is established given the diverse use cases expected for the network (general backup & sync, photo backup, video sharing, social media, websites etc etc). Are there examples of when web traffic, e.g. internet video uploads / cloud storage traffic all had a significant drop in demand for a prolonged time? 

I expect that, as the concept of node supply being unresponsive to increases in demand has been shown to be unrealistic, "demand droughts" that are significant enough to cause issues are unlikely to exist once demand is established.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1438984703221956789)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `20:11:39` **davidmc0** replied to jimcollinson:

> *jimcollinson said:*
> But then the cascade failure modes of a swing between demand positive to data drought, which we talk... [truncated]

Two more relevant points beyond questioning whether data droughts are likely to occur are:
1) Even if such a drought occurred, the problem causing a drought would be low demand, not insufficient supply, so the supply-stimulating emissions wouldn't help the problem of low demand. Maybe a demand-stimulating intervention would be better suited to that.
2) While node supply is elastic to demand increases (new nodes join quickly when store-cost is elevated), it's likely that it'll be less elastic to demand decreases, as operators leave them running hoping for future increases, or maintaining their share of the network revenues anticipating future token value increases. Basically, operators will have an incentive to add new nodes when demand is high, and an incentive to maintain nodes when demand is weak. If this turns out to be true, then during any temporary slow-down in demand, it's unlikely that a cascading failure due to node exits will happen.

"Nor the reality of a cold start."

Interesting. What are the concerns about a 'cold start' without emissions? I expect the community would provide sufficient nodes to get up and running ahead of demand growing that pool organically as data payments incentivise. Saying that, I'm sure the test of huge numbers of nodes enabled by emissions has been beneficial.

Good to hear some of the thinking around economics, but yes, in the end, it'll all be good if there is decent demand, and it'll be bad if there isn't 🙂

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1438984752047853730)

---

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `13:02:51` **jimcollinson** said:

 in this case, it's an issue with the client so how software interacts with the network, on a bug causing a little bit of confusion between the two… if you see what I mean

## Thursday, 2025-11-27

**[#🌐︱general-chat]** `10:07:25` **traktion0_20257** replied to jimcollinson:

> *jimcollinson said:*
> just to confirm, were aiming to do a release this week that will fix the problem

fwiw, I think we need a stronger production mindset for the network.

Imagine if there was data loss issues on Facebook, Instagram, LinkedIn, Youtube, etc, which went on for weeks. Compound that will little information coming out from the team, other than the occasional message like the above?

How about Cloudflare? Would they have let issues drift on for days at a time, without giving advise on how to circumvent the issues for sites depending on them?

At what point would regular production systems pivot to failover, if there was an ongoing issue? Within hours is likely, assuming reverting to the previous version was acceptable.

Usually staged/phased roll outs are desirable too. Non-breaking changes are a requirement, to allow easy roll back, with changes made over a number of releases where that isn't possible. Is it possible to roll back the client libs? Is it possible to roll back nodes?

Until these sort of things are taken seriously, the network isn't going to be considered for anything approaching production usage. Businesses can't just wait for weeks, even days, for these things to be corrected.

I understand the network is young, complex, pushing new boundaries, etc. However, clear/simple failover/rollback plans should be part of every release, especially if it is only an issue with the client side.

This comes from a place that cares. Please can we do more here.

[View in Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1209059621319221268/1209059622586163272/1443543731016958042)

---

But yeah, I do think we're getting closer and closer to the network needing to have a production mindset. Basically once we have called data perpetuallity or wider adoption, whichever comes first really.
